</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Formerly of</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Murder_Inc._(rap_group)" title="Murder Inc. (rap group)">Murder Inc.</a></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2">
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Musical artist</div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Jeffrey Bruce Atkins Sr.</b><sup id="cite_ref-twitter.com_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-twitter.com-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> (born February 29, 1976),<sup id="cite_ref-allmusic_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> better known by his stage name <b>Ja Rule</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt" lang="en-fonipa"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/dʒ/: &#39;j&#39; in &#39;jam&#39;">dʒ</span><span title="/ɑː/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;father&#39;">ɑː</span></span><span class="wrap"> </span><span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span><span title="/uː/: &#39;oo&#39; in &#39;goose&#39;">uː</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span></span>/</a></span></span>), is an American rapper. Born and raised in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, he debuted in 1999 with <i><a href="/wiki/Venni_Vetti_Vecci" title="Venni Vetti Vecci">Venni Vetti Vecci</a></i> and its lead single "<a href="/wiki/Holla_Holla" title="Holla Holla">Holla Holla</a>". During the 2000s, Ja Rule was signed to <a href="/wiki/Irv_Gotti" title="Irv Gotti">Irv Gotti</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Murder_Inc._Records" title="Murder Inc. Records">Murder Inc. Records</a>, formerly known as The Inc. From 1999 to 2005, Ja Rule had multiple hits that made the top 20 of the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> chart, including "<a href="/wiki/Between_Me_and_You" title="Between Me and You">Between Me and You</a>" (featuring <a href="/wiki/Christina_Milian" title="Christina Milian">Christina Milian</a>), "<a href="/wiki/I%27m_Real_(Murder_Remix)" class="mw-redirect" title="I&#39;m Real (Murder Remix)">I'm Real (Murder Remix)</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Ain%27t_It_Funny_(Murder_Remix)" title="Ain&#39;t It Funny (Murder Remix)">Ain't It Funny</a>" (both with <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Lopez" title="Jennifer Lopez">Jennifer Lopez</a>)—which both topped the Hot 100—the number 1 hit "<a href="/wiki/Always_on_Time" title="Always on Time">Always on Time</a>" (featuring <a href="/wiki/Ashanti_(singer)" title="Ashanti (singer)">Ashanti</a>), "<a href="/wiki/Mesmerize_(Ja_Rule_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mesmerize (Ja Rule song)">Mesmerize</a>" (featuring Ashanti), and "<a href="/wiki/Wonderful_(Ja_Rule_song)" title="Wonderful (Ja Rule song)">Wonderful</a>" (featuring <a href="/wiki/R._Kelly" title="R. Kelly">R. Kelly</a> and Ashanti).
</p><p>Ja Rule has been nominated for two <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards" title="American Music Awards">American Music Awards</a> and four <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Awards" title="Grammy Awards">Grammy Awards</a> with respective collaborators <a href="/wiki/Lil%27_Mo" title="Lil&#39; Mo">Lil' Mo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vita_(rapper)" title="Vita (rapper)">Vita</a>, Ashanti and <a href="/wiki/Case_(singer)" title="Case (singer)">Case</a>. Following the release of his <a href="/wiki/Platinum_record" class="mw-redirect" title="Platinum record">platinum</a>-selling debut <i>Venni Vetti Vecci</i> (1999), he released his respective second and third albums <i><a href="/wiki/Rule_3:36" title="Rule 3:36">Rule 3:36</a></i> (2000) and <i><a href="/wiki/Pain_Is_Love" title="Pain Is Love">Pain Is Love</a></i> (2001). Both albums topped the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200">US <i>Billboard</i> 200</a> album chart, launching him into the mainstream, selling over a combined 15 million units to a wide audience, and attaining triple platinum status from the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA), becoming his bestselling albums to date. Ja Rule followed up with his respective fourth, fifth and sixth albums <i><a href="/wiki/The_Last_Temptation_(Ja_Rule_album)" title="The Last Temptation (Ja Rule album)">The Last Temptation</a></i> (2002), <i><a href="/wiki/Blood_in_My_Eye" title="Blood in My Eye">Blood in My Eye</a></i> (2003), and <i><a href="/wiki/R.U.L.E." title="R.U.L.E.">R.U.L.E.</a></i> (2004), with <i>The Last Temptation</i> attaining platinum status and <i>R.U.L.E.</i> reaching <a href="/wiki/Gold_record" class="mw-redirect" title="Gold record">gold</a> status. As of 2018, Ja Rule has sold 14.4 million units in the US and has sold over 30 million records worldwide. In 2019, he joined the main cast of <a href="/wiki/We_TV" title="We TV">WeTV</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Growing_Up_Hip_Hop:_New_York" title="Growing Up Hip Hop: New York">Growing Up Hip Hop: New York</a></i>.
</p><p>Outside of music, Ja Rule attracted notable scrutiny for his involvement in the fraudulent <a href="/wiki/Fyre_Festival" title="Fyre Festival">Fyre Festival</a>, which he co-founded with <a href="/wiki/Con_artist" class="mw-redirect" title="Con artist">con artist</a> <a href="/wiki/Billy_McFarland_(fraudster)" class="mw-redirect" title="Billy McFarland (fraudster)">Billy McFarland</a>. In November 2019, he was cleared of any legal wrongdoing from his role in the festival.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ja_Rule&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Ja Rule was born Jeffrey Bruce Atkins on February 29, 1976, to Debra and Will in <a href="/wiki/Hollis,_Queens" title="Hollis, Queens">Hollis</a>, a section of the <a href="/wiki/Queens" title="Queens">Queens</a> borough of <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>. Jeffrey's father left the family when he was very young.<sup id="cite_ref-allmusic_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Atkins was raised as an only child, as his younger sister, Kristen, died in the womb when Atkins was 5.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> His mother, Debra, was a healthcare worker, and due to the amount of time she spent working, Atkins was largely raised by his grandparents as a <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witness" class="mw-redirect" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witness">Jehovah's Witness</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ebony_140_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ebony_140-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Atkins' mother left the Jehovah's Witness religion when he was 12.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Soon after, Atkins began selling drugs in <a href="/wiki/Hollis,_Queens" title="Hollis, Queens">Hollis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ja_Rule&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="Cash_Money_Click_.281994.E2.80.9395.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Cash_Money_Click_(1994–95)">Cash Money Click (1994–95)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ja_Rule&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Cash Money Click (1994–95)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Atkins began his rap career in 1994 with the hip hop group Cash Money Click alongside members Chris Black and O-1. He took the stage name "Ja Rule", telling <a href="/wiki/MTV_News" title="MTV News">MTV News</a> that the name came from a friend who addressed him by that name; other friends simply called him "Ja".<sup id="cite_ref-Rules_of_the_Game_2_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rules_of_the_Game_2-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Together they worked with producer <a href="/wiki/Irv_Gotti" title="Irv Gotti">DJ Irv</a> to produce a number of songs, releasing their debut single <i>"Get Tha Fortune"</i> independently in 1994. After the group signed with <a href="/wiki/TVT_Records" title="TVT Records">TVT Records</a>, the song was re-released through the label later that year as the B-side to their second single, <i>"4 My Click"</i>. "4 My Click" featured <a href="/wiki/Mic_Geronimo" title="Mic Geronimo">Mic Geronimo</a> and became popular on <a href="/wiki/Pirate_radio" title="Pirate radio">pirate radio</a>, eventually receiving airplay on <a href="/wiki/Yo!_MTV_Raps" title="Yo! MTV Raps">Yo! MTV Raps</a>. Plans for the release of the group's eponymous debut studio album were brought to a halt in 1995 after Chris Black was sentenced to five years in prison and the group was dropped from TVT, which led to their third single <i>"She Swallowed It"</i> never officially being released, however it was later bootlegged. With no label, the group disbanded shortly after being dropped.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Solo_career_and_Venni_Vetti_Vecci_.281995.E2.80.931999.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Solo_career_and_Venni_Vetti_Vecci_(1995–1999)">Solo career and <i>Venni Vetti Vecci</i> (1995–1999)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ja_Rule&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Solo career and Venni Vetti Vecci (1995–1999)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After being dropped from TVT, Ja Rule maintained a close relationship with DJ Irv, who was working as an executive producer for <a href="/wiki/Def_Jam_Recordings" title="Def Jam Recordings">Def Jam</a> at the time. DJ Irv, now known as <a href="/wiki/Irv_Gotti" title="Irv Gotti">Irv Gotti</a>, was hired as an <a href="/wiki/Artists_and_repertoire" title="Artists and repertoire">A&amp;R</a> for the label and was able to get Ja Rule a contract with Def Jam.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> In 1995, he made his first solo appearance on Mic Geronimo's "Time to Build" alongside <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a> and <a href="/wiki/DMX_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="DMX (rapper)">DMX</a>, who were also in their early stages of their careers. He later appeared on the song "Usual Suspects" from Mic Geronimo's second album <a href="/wiki/Vendetta_(Mic_Geronimo_album)" title="Vendetta (Mic Geronimo album)">Vendetta</a> in 1997, alongside <a href="/wiki/The_Lox" title="The Lox">The Lox</a>, DMX and <a href="/wiki/Tragedy_Khadafi" title="Tragedy Khadafi">Tragedy Khadafi</a>. He also had a brief cameo in the video for "Walk In New York" by Queens hardcore rap group <a href="/wiki/Onyx_(hip_hop_group)" title="Onyx (hip hop group)">Onyx</a>. Later in 1997, Irv Gotti was granted his own imprint from Def Jam, known as <a href="/wiki/Murder_Inc._Records" title="Murder Inc. Records">Murder Inc. Records</a>. Ja Rule was promoted as the label's flagship artist, and he continued to make guest appearances on songs by other artists, including <a href="/wiki/Method_Man" title="Method Man">Method Man</a>, <a href="/wiki/Redman_(rapper)" title="Redman (rapper)">Redman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nas" title="Nas">Nas</a>, DMX, <a href="/wiki/LL_Cool_J" title="LL Cool J">LL Cool J</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dru_Hill" title="Dru Hill">Dru Hill</a>. He later appeared on Jay-Z's 1998 hit single "<a href="/wiki/Can_I_Get_A..." title="Can I Get A...">Can I Get A...</a>", for which he wrote the hook. It was originally planned to be Ja Rule's debut single until Jay-Z heard the track and requested it for himself. During this time, he rapped under the slightly modified stage name <b>Jah</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Returning to the Ja Rule name, his debut single <a href="/wiki/Holla_Holla" title="Holla Holla">Holla Holla</a> was released in March 1999 and became a hit, peaking at #35 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100">Billboard Hot 100</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-singles_charts_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-singles_charts-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Fueled by the success of Holla Holla, Ja Rule's debut album, <i><a href="/wiki/Venni_Vetti_Vecci" title="Venni Vetti Vecci">Venni Vetti Vecci</a></i>, was released in 1999, peaking at #3 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> with 184,000 copies sold in its first week. It eventually reached platinum status in the US due to the popularity of "Holla Holla".<sup id="cite_ref-RIAA_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> A remix of "Holla Holla" was later released, featuring Jay-Z, <a href="/wiki/Vita_(rapper)" title="Vita (rapper)">Vita</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caddillac_Tah_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="Caddillac Tah (rapper)">Cadillac Tah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Black_Child" title="Black Child">Black Child</a>, <a href="/wiki/Memphis_Bleek" title="Memphis Bleek">Memphis Bleek</a> and <a href="/wiki/Busta_Rhymes" title="Busta Rhymes">Busta Rhymes</a>.
</p>
<h3><span id="Rule_3:36.2C_Pain_Is_Love_and_The_Last_Temptation_.282000.E2.80.932002.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Rule_3:36,_Pain_Is_Love_and_The_Last_Temptation_(2000–2002)"><i>Rule 3:36</i>, <i>Pain Is Love</i> and <i>The Last Temptation</i> (2000–2002)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ja_Rule&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Rule 3:36, Pain Is Love and The Last Temptation (2000–2002)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Vita%26Ja.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Vita%26Ja.jpg/181px-Vita%26Ja.jpg" decoding="async" width="181" height="214" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9d/Vita%26Ja.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="261" data-file-height="308" /></a><figcaption>Ja Rule and <a href="/wiki/Vita_(rapper)" title="Vita (rapper)">Vita</a> in 2001</figcaption></figure>
<p>Ja Rule's second single, "<a href="/wiki/Between_Me_and_You" title="Between Me and You">Between Me and You</a>", featuring <a href="/wiki/Christina_Milian" title="Christina Milian">Christina Milian</a>, was released in June 2000 as the first single from his second studio album and became his first major crossover hit, earning Top 40 airplay and reaching #11 on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100. The album's next single, "Put It on Me", featuring <a href="/wiki/Vita_(rapper)" title="Vita (rapper)">Vita</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lil%27_Mo" title="Lil&#39; Mo">Lil' Mo</a>, was released in December 2000 and became one of the biggest hits of 2001, reaching #8 on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 and becoming the first top 10 hit for both Ja Rule and Vita.<sup id="cite_ref-singles_charts_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-singles_charts-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> The video for "Put It on Me" also topped the MTV Video Countdown for a week, and became the first music video to be retired on <a href="/wiki/Black_Entertainment_Television" class="mw-redirect" title="Black Entertainment Television">BET</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/106_%26_Park" title="106 &amp; Park">106 &amp; Park</a></i> after spending more than 60 days on the countdown. The video also ranked #1 on BET's <i>Notarized: Top 100 Videos of 2001</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Ja Rule's second album, <i><a href="/wiki/Rule_3:36" title="Rule 3:36">Rule 3:36</a></i>, was released on October 10, 2000, and went in a much different stylistic direction from Venni Vetti Vecci, changing his almost trademark hardcore hip-hop sound to mainstream-oriented <a href="/wiki/Pop-rap" class="mw-redirect" title="Pop-rap">pop-rap</a>, debuting at #1 on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> with 276,000 copies sold in its first week, making it Ja Rule's first number one album. The album later went on to be certified triple platinum by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA).<sup id="cite_ref-RIAA_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The success of Rule 3:36 promoted Ja Rule to international status, and made Murder Inc. one of the biggest labels in the United States. The same success followed with his third album, which spawned three top 10 singles, two of them reaching #1. The first, "<a href="/wiki/Livin%27_It_Up_(Ja_Rule_song)" title="Livin&#39; It Up (Ja Rule song)">Livin' It Up</a>", featuring <a href="/wiki/Case_(singer)" title="Case (singer)">Case</a>, was released in July 2001 and reached #6 on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> It also achieved success in the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, reaching #5 on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart" title="UK Singles Chart">UK Singles Chart</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The second single, "<a href="/wiki/Always_on_Time" title="Always on Time">Always on Time</a>", was released in October 2001 and marked the first major guest appearance for Murder Inc's youngest artist <a href="/wiki/Ashanti_(singer)" title="Ashanti (singer)">Ashanti</a>, and became both Ja Rule and Ashanti's first song to top the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100.<sup id="cite_ref-singles_charts_17-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-singles_charts-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The remix of <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Lopez" title="Jennifer Lopez">Jennifer Lopez</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/I%27m_Real_(Jennifer_Lopez_song)" title="I&#39;m Real (Jennifer Lopez song)">I'm Real</a>" featuring Ja Rule was included on the album and topped the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 for five non-consecutive weeks, beginning September 8, 2001, and also topped the Hot 100 Airplay chart. The song was a staple of <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a>/<a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip hop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">pop</a> radio during the summer and fall of 2001, spending fifteen weeks total in the top five of the Hot 100. In 2009 the single was named the 30th most successful song of the 2000s, on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 Songs of the Decade.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The album's fourth single, "<a href="/wiki/Down_Ass_Bitch" title="Down Ass Bitch">Down Ass Bitch</a>" featuring <a href="/wiki/Charli_Baltimore" title="Charli Baltimore">Charli Baltimore</a> was also successful, reaching #21 on the Hot 100.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Ja Rule released his third studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Pain_Is_Love" title="Pain Is Love">Pain Is Love</a></i>, on October 2, 2001. Like its predecessor, <i>Pain Is Love</i> topped the <i>Billboard</i> 200 with first-week sales of 361,000 copies and is certified triple platinum by the RIAA.<sup id="cite_ref-RIAA_18-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> The album also received a <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammy Award">Grammy</a> nomination in 2002 for <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap Album">Best Rap Album</a>. By 2007, 3.6 million copies of <i>Pain Is Love</i> had been sold.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Last_Temptation_(Ja_Rule_album)" title="The Last Temptation (Ja Rule album)">The Last Temptation</a></i>, Ja Rule's fourth album, was released on November 19, 2002. It spawned two hit singles, "<a href="/wiki/Thug_Lovin%27" title="Thug Lovin&#39;">Thug Lovin'</a>", featuring <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Brown" title="Bobby Brown">Bobby Brown</a>, which peaked at #42 on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100, and "<a href="/wiki/Mesmerize_(Ja_Rule_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mesmerize (Ja Rule song)">Mesmerize</a>", a duet with Ashanti that peaked at #2 on the Billboard Hot 100.<sup id="cite_ref-singles_charts_17-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-singles_charts-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> <i>The Last Temptation</i> debuted at #4 on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 with first-week sales of 237,000 copies and was certified platinum by the RIAA in December 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-RIAA_18-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-album_charts_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-album_charts-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="50_Cent_feud.2C_Blood_in_My_Eye_and_R.U.L.E._.282003.E2.80.932004.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="50_Cent_feud,_Blood_in_My_Eye_and_R.U.L.E._(2003–2004)">50 Cent feud, <i>Blood in My Eye</i> and <i>R.U.L.E.</i> (2003–2004)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ja_Rule&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 50 Cent feud, Blood in My Eye and R.U.L.E. (2003–2004)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:KexEdit-0.8.6.png.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/KexEdit-0.8.6.png.jpg/220px-KexEdit-0.8.6.png.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/KexEdit-0.8.6.png.jpg/330px-KexEdit-0.8.6.png.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/KexEdit-0.8.6.png.jpg/440px-KexEdit-0.8.6.png.jpg 2x" data-file-width="480" data-file-height="480" /></a><figcaption>Ja Rule (left) in 2000 with <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_McGriff" title="Kenneth McGriff">Kenneth "Supreme" McGriff</a>, a notorious <a href="/wiki/Queens,_New_York" class="mw-redirect" title="Queens, New York">Queens</a> gangster closely affiliated with <a href="/wiki/Irv_Gotti" title="Irv Gotti">Irv Gotti</a> and <a href="/wiki/Murder_Inc._Records" title="Murder Inc. Records">Murder Inc. Records</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>Shortly after the release of his fourth studio album, Ja Rule's ongoing beef with fellow Queens rapper <a href="/wiki/50_Cent" title="50 Cent">50 Cent</a> reached its peak, with both artists taking to radio stations almost daily to trade insults and diss tracks.<sup id="cite_ref-http&#58;//hiphopdx.com_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-http://hiphopdx.com-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MTV_News_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV_News-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-xxlmag.com_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xxlmag.com-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-hiphopdx.com_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hiphopdx.com-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MTV_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> On January 3, 2003, the Murder Inc. offices were raided by <a href="/wiki/FBI" class="mw-redirect" title="FBI">FBI</a> agents and <a href="/wiki/NYPD" class="mw-redirect" title="NYPD">NYPD</a> officers due to accusations of money laundering and drug trades toward <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_McGriff" title="Kenneth McGriff">Kenneth "Supreme" McGriff</a>, who was associated with Irv Gotti.<sup id="cite_ref-billboard.com_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billboard.com-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Due to the federal investigation, Ja Rule had a late response in his beef with 50 Cent.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> By association, 50 Cent's labelmates <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Obie_Trice" title="Obie Trice">Obie Trice</a>, <a href="/wiki/D12" title="D12">D12</a>, and Ja Rule's former friends and associates <a href="/wiki/DMX_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="DMX (rapper)">DMX</a> and <a href="/wiki/Busta_Rhymes" title="Busta Rhymes">Busta Rhymes</a> were brought into the feud too. Ja Rule released the diss track <i>"Loose Change"</i> in April 2003, where he attacks 50 Cent, as well as Eminem, Busta Rhymes and <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> 50 Cent eventually responded with <i>"Hail Mary"</i>, which used the beat from <a href="/wiki/2Pac" class="mw-redirect" title="2Pac">2Pac</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Hail_Mary_(2Pac_song)" title="Hail Mary (2Pac song)">song of the same name</a> and featured Eminem and Busta Rhymes.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> The beef continued to be highly publicized throughout 2003, and eventually led to Ja Rule meeting with Minister <a href="/wiki/Louis_Farrakhan" title="Louis Farrakhan">Louis Farrakhan</a> in October, who wanted to intervene and prevent escalating violence in the feud.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Ja Rule's fifth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Blood_in_My_Eye" title="Blood in My Eye">Blood in My Eye</a></i>, was released on November 4, 2003, under the Murder Inc. label, which renamed itself "The Inc." several days after the album release. The material was intended simply as a mixtape, but was released as an album to fulfill Ja Rule's contractual commitment to Murder Inc. to release one annually. The album was described as a "hate" album directed at various rappers, including 50 Cent, <a href="/wiki/G-Unit" title="G-Unit">G-Unit</a>, Eminem, <a href="/wiki/Proof_(rapper)" title="Proof (rapper)">Proof</a>, Dr. Dre, DMX, Busta Rhymes and others, and marked a return to the <a href="/wiki/Hardcore_hip-hop" class="mw-redirect" title="Hardcore hip-hop">hardcore style</a> Ja Rule had used in his earlier career. It spawned one hit single, "Clap Back", which reached #44 on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 and won a Source Award for "Fat Tape" song of the year. It peaked at #6 on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 200, selling 139,000 copies in its first week of release, and had sold over 468,000 copies in the U.S. by 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-album_charts_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-album_charts-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Ja Rule's sixth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/R.U.L.E." title="R.U.L.E.">R.U.L.E.</a></i>, was released in November 2004, debuting at #7 and selling 166,000 copies in its first week of release. Its lead single, "<a href="/wiki/Wonderful_(Ja_Rule_song)" title="Wonderful (Ja Rule song)">Wonderful</a>", featuring <a href="/wiki/R._Kelly" title="R. Kelly">R. Kelly</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ashanti_(entertainer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ashanti (entertainer)">Ashanti</a>, peaked at #5 on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100. The single was followed by the street anthem "<a href="/wiki/New_York_(Ja_Rule_song)" title="New York (Ja Rule song)">New York</a>", featuring <a href="/wiki/Fat_Joe" title="Fat Joe">Fat Joe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jadakiss" title="Jadakiss">Jadakiss</a>, which charted at #27 on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100. The third single was the love song "<a href="/wiki/Caught_Up_(Ja_Rule_song)" title="Caught Up (Ja Rule song)">Caught Up</a>", featuring <a href="/wiki/Lloyd_(singer)" title="Lloyd (singer)">Lloyd</a>, which had failed to make an impact on the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100. The RIAA certified <i>R.U.L.E.</i> Gold on January 14, 2005,<sup id="cite_ref-RIAA_18-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> and by October 2007 the album had sold 658,000 copies.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Hiatus.2C_departure_from_Def_Jam.2C_decline_of_The_Inc._Records_.282005.E2.80.9309.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Hiatus,_departure_from_Def_Jam,_decline_of_The_Inc._Records_(2005–09)">Hiatus, departure from Def Jam, decline of The Inc. Records (2005–09)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ja_Rule&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Hiatus, departure from Def Jam, decline of The Inc. Records (2005–09)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Ja_Rule_Fort_Hood.JPEG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Ja_Rule_Fort_Hood.JPEG/220px-Ja_Rule_Fort_Hood.JPEG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Ja_Rule_Fort_Hood.JPEG/330px-Ja_Rule_Fort_Hood.JPEG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Ja_Rule_Fort_Hood.JPEG/440px-Ja_Rule_Fort_Hood.JPEG 2x" data-file-width="3003" data-file-height="2002" /></a><figcaption>Ja Rule performing in <a href="/wiki/Fort_Hood" class="mw-redirect" title="Fort Hood">Fort Hood</a>, <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>, May 13, 2005</figcaption></figure>
<p>On December 6, 2005, The Inc. released <i><a href="/wiki/Exodus_(Ja_Rule_album)" title="Exodus (Ja Rule album)">Exodus</a></i>, a greatest hits album whose only new tracks were the song "Me" and intro and <a href="/wiki/Outro_(music)" class="mw-redirect" title="Outro (music)">outro</a> tracks. <i>Exodus</i> was the last album on Ja Rule's contract with The Inc. After its release, Ja Rule took a hiatus from recording music.<sup id="cite_ref-allmusic_3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allmusic-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Meanwhile, <a href="/wiki/The_Inc._Records" class="mw-redirect" title="The Inc. Records">The Inc. Records</a> was still under investigation because of alleged drug trades with Kenneth "Supreme" McGriff.<sup id="cite_ref-billboard.com_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-billboard.com-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> This led to Def Jam Recordings refusing to renew The Inc.'s contract. From 2005 to 2006, Gotti searched for other labels, finally reaching a deal with <a href="/wiki/Universal_Records" class="mw-redirect" title="Universal Records">Universal Records</a> (part of the same company as Def Jam). A few years later The Inc. left Universal Records due to business issues and failure to secure funds for projects.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> In 2007, Ja Rule founded record label <b>Mpire Music Group</b>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Pain_Is_Love_2.2C_prison.2C_and_release_.282011.E2.80.932013.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Pain_Is_Love_2,_prison,_and_release_(2011–2013)"><i>Pain Is Love 2</i>, prison, and release (2011–2013)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ja_Rule&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Pain Is Love 2, prison, and release (2011–2013)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In February 2011, it was announced that Ja Rule had started working on a new album, <i><a href="/wiki/Pain_Is_Love_2" title="Pain Is Love 2">Pain Is Love 2</a></i>, to be produced by the producers of the original <i>Pain Is Love</i> album to "recreate magic". Most of the production was to be done by <a href="/wiki/Channel_7_(musician)" title="Channel 7 (musician)">7 Aurelius</a> (who co-produced "<a href="/wiki/Down_Ass_Bitch" title="Down Ass Bitch">Down Ass Bitch</a>"), while Irv Gotti was to be executive producer. Ja Rule had planned on releasing it on June 7, 2011, but decided to delay the release in order to allow more time to perfect the "level and quality of the records" and to avoid "doing an injustice to [his] fans".<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> A revised release date of October 11, 2011, was also pushed back.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> During the delay, Ja Rule released a new track, "Falling to Pieces", produced by 7 Aurelius, which samples <a href="/wiki/The_Script" title="The Script">The Script</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Breakeven_(song)" title="Breakeven (song)">Breakeven</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> On October 2, 2011, another track, "Spun a Web", was released, also produced by 7 Aurelius and sampling <a href="/wiki/Coldplay" title="Coldplay">Coldplay</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Trouble_(Coldplay_song)" title="Trouble (Coldplay song)">Trouble</a>". The following day a teaser video premiered on YouTube, and the official video was released on October 11.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> <i>Pain Is Love 2</i> was finally released on February 28, 2012, by which time Ja Rule was serving a two-year sentence in prison for gun possession and tax evasion.
</p><p>Ja Rule was released from prison on May 7, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-JA_RULE_RELEASED_From_Prison_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JA_RULE_RELEASED_From_Prison-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Alongside Lil Wayne and Birdman, he appeared on the remix of the track "She Tried", which appeared on the <a href="/wiki/N.O.R.E" class="mw-redirect" title="N.O.R.E">N.O.R.E</a> album <i><a href="/wiki/Student_of_the_Game" title="Student of the Game">Student of the Game</a>.</i> On September 18, 2013, Ja Rule released a track titled "Fresh Out Da Pen". The track had first premiered on <a href="/wiki/WQHT" title="WQHT">Hot 97</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> A few days later he released "Everything". Both tracks were produced by Visionary producers Reefa and Myles William. On September 27, 2013, both tracks were released on iTunes for digital download.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> In September 2013, it was confirmed that Ja Rule and Gotti had relaunched <a href="/wiki/Murder_Inc_Records" class="mw-redirect" title="Murder Inc Records">Murder Inc Records</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Memoir.2C_reality_show_and_future_projects_.282014.E2.80.93present.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Memoir,_reality_show_and_future_projects_(2014–present)">Memoir, reality show and future projects (2014–present)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ja_Rule&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Memoir, reality show and future projects (2014–present)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2014, Ja Rule released a memoir, <i>Unruly: The Highs and Lows of Becoming a Man</i>, in which he reflected on his past struggles with a difficult adolescence in New York City and everything that followed, from breakout success and destructive rivalries to fatherhood and a two-year prison sentence.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> In July 2014, Ja Rule announced his eighth studio album, which was eventually pushed back to a 2016 release.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> Also in 2014, MTV announced that Ja Rule and his family would star in the upcoming reality show <i>Follow the Rules</i> which was co-produced by <a href="/wiki/Queen_Latifah" title="Queen Latifah">Queen Latifah</a>. A sneak peek trailer of the show surfaced on the internet in September 2014 and the show premiered on October 26, 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> In October 2015, Rule announced that he and Gotti had partnered with <a href="/wiki/Paramount_Pictures" title="Paramount Pictures">Paramount Pictures</a> on a TV drama series based on the history of Murder Inc., set to premiere in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> In February 2016, Ja Rule announced that his upcoming eighth studio album would be titled <i>Coup De Grâce</i><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> and would be his last album.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> In December 2016, he appeared on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hamilton_Mixtape" title="The Hamilton Mixtape">The Hamilton Mixtape</a></i>, rapping Hamilton's verse in <a href="/wiki/Ashanti_(singer)" title="Ashanti (singer)">Ashanti</a>'s performance of "<a href="/wiki/Helpless_(Hamilton_song)" title="Helpless (Hamilton song)">Helpless</a>", referencing <a href="/wiki/Lin-Manuel_Miranda" title="Lin-Manuel Miranda">Lin-Manuel Miranda</a>'s impression of him in the last line of that verse. On June 26, 2018, Ashanti confirmed that she and Ja Rule are working on a collaborative album.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On October 15, 2021, in celebration of the twentieth anniversary of the release of his third studio album, <i>Pain is Love</i>, Ja Rule released the single, "Sincerely, Jeffrey"<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> for all streaming platforms.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Acting">Acting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ja_Rule&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Acting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p>His first film was a buddy movie with <a href="/wiki/Pras" title="Pras">Pras</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Turn_It_Up_(film)" title="Turn It Up (film)">Turn It Up</a></i>; he appeared in a minor role in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Fast_and_the_Furious_(2001_film)" title="The Fast and the Furious (2001 film)">The Fast and the Furious</a></i>. He appeared in several movies including <i><a href="/wiki/Back_in_the_Day_(2005_film)" title="Back in the Day (2005 film)">Back in the Day</a></i> with <a href="/wiki/Ving_Rhames" title="Ving Rhames">Ving Rhames</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pam_Grier" title="Pam Grier">Pam Grier</a> and <i><a href="/wiki/Half_Past_Dead" title="Half Past Dead">Half Past Dead</a></i> as <a href="/wiki/Steven_Seagal" title="Steven Seagal">Steven Seagal</a>'s co-star. He also starred in the movies <i><a href="/wiki/The_Cookout" title="The Cookout">The Cookout</a></i> with <a href="/wiki/Queen_Latifah" title="Queen Latifah">Queen Latifah</a> and <i><a href="/wiki/Assault_on_Precinct_13_(2005_film)" title="Assault on Precinct 13 (2005 film)">Assault on Precinct 13</a></i>. In 2013, he starred in <i><a href="/wiki/I%27m_in_Love_with_a_Church_Girl" title="I&#39;m in Love with a Church Girl">I'm in Love with a Church Girl</a></i>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_ventures">Other ventures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ja_Rule&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Other ventures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2004, Ja Rule and Gotti launched an urban clothing line called <i>ErvinGeoffrey</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> In 2006, Ja Rule launched a liquor company, The Mojito.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2015, Ja Rule partnered with <a href="/wiki/Billy_McFarland_(fraudster)" class="mw-redirect" title="Billy McFarland (fraudster)">Billy McFarland</a>, the CEO of the credit card service company Magnises, to become its creative head and spokesman.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> In August 2015, Ja Rule collaborated with footwear businessman <a href="/wiki/Steve_Madden" title="Steve Madden">Steve Madden</a> on a new line of men's sneakers called <i>Maven x Madden</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> which were released for sale by fall 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2016, Ja Rule co-founded <i>Fyre Media, Inc.</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> a talent booking agency, with Billy McFarland. In April 2017, the venture touted its <a href="/wiki/Fyre_Festival" title="Fyre Festival">Fyre Festival</a> in Hamilton, Bahamas, as a luxury event, but it was fraudulent,<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> disappointing hundreds of ticket-buyers.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Rule and McFarland faced a $100 million class action suit.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2020, Ja Rule developed a live-streaming app called "Iconn Live".<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> The app debuted on <a href="/wiki/Apple_TV" title="Apple TV">Apple TV</a> in November 2022.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2021, Ja Rule partnered with a team of software engineers to launch Flipkick, a platform focusing on selling physical works of art as <a href="/wiki/Non-fungible_token" title="Non-fungible token">non-fungible tokens</a>. Flipkick claims to be "the first company to offer cryptographic authentication of physical works of art sold as and linked to NFTs." To inaugurate the platform, Ja Rule listed for auction a painting he commissioned in 2012 by artist Tripp Derrick Barnes depicting the Fyre Media Inc logo. The painting was listed with an estimate of $600,000.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2023, Ja Rule launched a premium <a href="/wiki/Wine" title="Wine">wine</a> label called <i>Rose Vine Cellars</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ja_Rule&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Atkins earned his <a href="/wiki/GED" class="mw-redirect" title="GED">GED</a> while in prison in February 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> In February 2021, Atkins completed an online course at <a href="/wiki/Harvard_Business_School" title="Harvard Business School">Harvard Business School</a> and shared a photo of his certificate of completion on <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">Twitter</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Family">Family</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ja_Rule&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Family">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In April 2001, Ja Rule married Aisha Murray.<sup id="cite_ref-Ebony_142_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ebony_142-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> The couple have three children: Brittney Asja Atkins (born 1995), Jeffrey Jr. (born 2000), and Jordan (born 2003).<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ja_Rule&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Raised as a <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witness" class="mw-redirect" title="Jehovah&#39;s Witness">Jehovah's Witness</a> for most of his childhood, Ja Rule identifies as a <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christian</a>. He "reconnected with God" in 2013 while promoting the movie <i>I'm in Love with a Church Girl</i>. He was <a href="/wiki/Baptism" title="Baptism">baptized</a>, along with his wife, in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_issues">Legal issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ja_Rule&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Legal issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 2003, he allegedly punched a man in Toronto, who later sued. He received a $1,200 fine after pleading guilty to assault.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2004, police investigated whether a feud involving <a href="/wiki/Murder_Inc_Records" class="mw-redirect" title="Murder Inc Records">Murder Inc.</a> led to a fatal shooting outside a nightclub party hosted by Ja Rule and Leon Richardson.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On July 1, 2004, Ja Rule was arrested for driving with a suspended license and possessing marijuana.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2007, Ja Rule was arrested for gun and drug possession charges along with <a href="/wiki/Lil_Wayne" title="Lil Wayne">Lil Wayne</a>, who served eight months in prison during 2010 for attempted possession of a weapon stemming from the arrest.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nydn_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nydn-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> The court rejected Ja Rule's argument that the gun was illegally obtained evidence.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On December 13, 2010, Ja Rule received a two-year prison sentence after pleading guilty to attempted possession of a weapon after the aforementioned 2007 arrest. On March 8, 2011, Ja Rule's surrender date for his two-year prison sentence was set for June 8.<sup id="cite_ref-test_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-test-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> He was first sent to <a href="/wiki/Rikers_Island" title="Rikers Island">Rikers Island</a>, then later to a state facility in <a href="/wiki/Upstate_New_York" title="Upstate New York">Upstate New York</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2011, Ja Rule received an additional 28-month prison sentence for tax evasion, to run concurrently with his state term, failing to pay taxes on more than $3 million in earnings between 2004 and 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> He was released from state prison on February 21, 2013, but was immediately taken into federal custody for the tax case, for which he had less than six months remaining on his sentence.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> Ja Rule was held in Brooklyn's <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Detention_Center,_Brooklyn" title="Metropolitan Detention Center, Brooklyn">Metropolitan Detention Center</a> and was set to be released on July 28, 2013. Ja Rule was released from prison early on May 7, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-JA_RULE_RELEASED_From_Prison_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JA_RULE_RELEASED_From_Prison-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By July 1, 2017, Ja Rule faced more than a dozen lawsuits filed by ticket buyers and investors in the failed <a href="/wiki/Fyre_Festival" title="Fyre Festival">Fyre Festival</a> and his partner in the venture, <a href="/wiki/Billy_McFarland_(entrepreneur)" class="mw-redirect" title="Billy McFarland (entrepreneur)">Billy McFarland</a>, had been indicted for fraud.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> In November 2019, charges were reportedly dropped against Ja Rule in connection with the lawsuits.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Feuds">Feuds</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ja_Rule&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Feuds">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="50_Cent">50 Cent</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ja_Rule&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: 50 Cent">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Before signing with <a href="/wiki/Interscope_Records" title="Interscope Records">Interscope Records</a>, rapper <a href="/wiki/50_Cent" title="50 Cent">50 Cent</a> engaged in a well-publicized feud with Ja Rule and his label <a href="/wiki/Murder_Inc._Records" title="Murder Inc. Records">Murder Inc. Records</a>. 50 Cent claimed that the feud began in 1999 after Ja Rule spotted him with a man who robbed him of his jewelry and also because Ja Rule was "trying to be Tupac".<sup id="cite_ref-http&#58;//hiphopdx.com_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-http://hiphopdx.com-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> However, Ja Rule claimed the conflict stemmed from a video shoot in <a href="/wiki/Queens" title="Queens">Queens</a> because 50 Cent did not like Ja Rule "getting so much love" from the neighborhood.<sup id="cite_ref-MTV_News_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV_News-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> 50 Cent indirectly confirmed this in an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/XXL_Magazine" class="mw-redirect" title="XXL Magazine">XXL Magazine</a></i>, where 50 Cent states he was upset with Ja Rule for being under the aegis of <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_%22Supreme%22_McGriff" class="mw-redirect" title="Kenneth &quot;Supreme&quot; McGriff">Kenneth "Supreme" McGriff</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-xxlmag.com_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-xxlmag.com-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> A confrontation occurred in Atlanta in which Ja Rule claims he struck 50 Cent with a baseball bat, later his crew stepping in to beat up 50 Cent.<sup id="cite_ref-hiphopdx.com_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hiphopdx.com-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Another confrontation occurred while in a <a href="/wiki/The_Hit_Factory" title="The Hit Factory">New York studio</a> where rapper <a href="/wiki/Black_Child_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="Black Child (rapper)">Black Child</a>, a Murder Inc. artist, stabbed 50 Cent, causing a wound requiring four <a href="/wiki/Surgical_suture" title="Surgical suture">stitches</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MTV_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In his book, 50 Cent details how Kenneth "Supreme" McGriff tried to resolve the conflict between him and Ja Rule. Allegedly, McGriff asked 50 Cent to leave them alone because of the money involved. 50 Cent insinuated the conflict had something to do with the shooting where he was ambushed and shot.
</p><p>Since then, Black Child and other Murder Inc. rappers such as <a href="/wiki/Caddillac_Tah_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="Caddillac Tah (rapper)">Cadillac Tah</a> publicly insulted 50 Cent with "There's a Snitch in the Club" by Cadillac Tah, and "The Real Wanksta" by Black Child. In both songs, Black Child details violent actions directed toward 50 Cent.<sup id="cite_ref-MTV_32-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> The exchange of insult tracks released from both parties culminated in Ja Rule's <i><a href="/wiki/Blood_in_My_Eye" title="Blood in My Eye">Blood in My Eye</a></i>, which was an album that returned additional insults to 50 Cent. Because of the ongoing feud between the two, 50 Cent's labelmates <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Obie_Trice" title="Obie Trice">Obie Trice</a>, <a href="/wiki/D12" title="D12">D12</a>, <a href="/wiki/DMX_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="DMX (rapper)">DMX</a>, <a href="/wiki/Busta_Rhymes" title="Busta Rhymes">Busta Rhymes</a>, and the rest of the members of <a href="/wiki/G-Unit" title="G-Unit">G-Unit</a>, also became involved and released tracks which insulted Ja Rule.<sup id="cite_ref-MTV_32-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Ja Rule later released <i><a href="/wiki/R.U.L.E." title="R.U.L.E.">R.U.L.E.</a></i> which included the successful single "New York", featuring <a href="/wiki/Jadakiss" title="Jadakiss">Jadakiss</a> and Fat Joe, in which Ja Rule obliquely attacked 50 Cent. This single prompted 50 Cent to enter a feud with the two featured artists, reflected in his response, "<a href="/wiki/Piggy_Bank_(song)" title="Piggy Bank (song)">Piggy Bank</a>".
</p><p>Although it seemed that the feud was over, Ja Rule returned with a track titled "21 Gunz".<sup id="cite_ref-illseed_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-illseed-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> In response, <a href="/wiki/Lloyd_Banks" title="Lloyd Banks">Lloyd Banks</a> and 50 Cent released the track "Return of Ja Fool" on Lloyd Banks' mixtape <i>Mo Money in the Bank Pt. 4, Gang Green Season Starts Now</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-illseed_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-illseed-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In an interview with MTV, Ja Rule stated, in reference to his album, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Mirror_(Ja_Rule_album)" title="The Mirror (Ja Rule album)">The Mirror</a></i>:
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>There was a lot of things I wanted to say, and I didn't want there to be any bitter records on the album. Because I'm not bitter about anything that happened [in the past few years].<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>In May 2011, it was confirmed that both Ja Rule and 50 Cent had ended the feud. Ja Rule said, "I'm cool. We ain't beefing no more. We'll never collaborate. That's just what it is. You don't have to be at war with somebody, but it's also kind of like U.S. and another country that they may not get along with. We don't gotta go to war, but we're not friends either. But we can coincide inside of a world. He's doing him, and he's not thinking about me, and I'm doing me and I'm not thinking about him."
</p><p>In September 2013, in an interview with <a href="/wiki/Angie_Martinez" title="Angie Martinez">Angie Martinez</a> on The Angie Martinez show on HOT 97, both Rule and <a href="/wiki/Irv_Gotti" title="Irv Gotti">Irv Gotti</a> acknowledged 50 Cent not only took a toll on Ja Rule's prominence, but along with the federal indictment, damaged Murder, Inc., as a music label. They told Martinez their immediate reaction on hearing 50 Cent's single, "<a href="/wiki/In_Da_Club" class="mw-redirect" title="In Da Club">In Da Club</a>", on the radio was that it was "so dope" and that they had a problem with it. They also disclosed that they had been blackballed from various award shows where 50 Cent was to perform due to their feud. Notwithstanding seeing 50 Cent as a hustler, they liked his entrepreneurial mentality, 10 years on, no longer had a problem with him. Ja Rule indicated he had plans to write a book surrounding the whole experience.
<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In early 2018, after four years of taunting Ja Rule, 50 Cent reiginited the beef after he publicly dissed him on <a href="/wiki/Big_Boy_(radio_host)" title="Big Boy (radio host)">Big Boy</a>'s Neighborhood, leading to Ja Rule retaliating on Twitter the next day.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="Shady.2FAftermath"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Shady/Aftermath">Shady/Aftermath</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ja_Rule&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Shady/Aftermath">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The conflict started after <a href="/wiki/50_Cent" title="50 Cent">50 Cent</a> signed to <a href="/wiki/Shady_Records" title="Shady Records">Shady Records</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aftermath_Entertainment" title="Aftermath Entertainment">Aftermath</a> in 2002. Ja Rule and Irv Gotti expressed dissatisfaction with <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a> for signing an artist with whom they were in conflict and threatened to take action against them if they released any 50 Cent tracks deprecatory of Murder Inc.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The conflict escalated when Ja Rule released "Loose Change" attacking 50 Cent, Eminem and Dr. Dre. The song also includes lyrics that insulted Eminem's family (most notably his then 7-year-old daughter Hailie Jade) and acquaintances.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceB_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceB-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> In response, Eminem, <a href="/wiki/D12" title="D12">D12</a> and <a href="/wiki/Obie_Trice" title="Obie Trice">Obie Trice</a> released the deprecatory track "Hailie's Revenge (Doe Rae Mi)" featuring vocals from Eminem's daughter.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Busta_Rhymes" title="Busta Rhymes">Busta Rhymes</a> joined the conflict when he was featured on the track "Hail Mary 2003" with Eminem and 50 Cent.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> The song, which is a remake of <a href="/wiki/Tupac_Shakur" title="Tupac Shakur">Tupac Shakur</a>'s song "<a href="/wiki/Hail_Mary_(2Pac_song)" title="Hail Mary (2Pac song)">Hail Mary</a>", was done partially as a response to Ja Rule's remake of Tupac's song, "<a href="/wiki/Pain_(Tupac_Shakur_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pain (Tupac Shakur song)">Pain</a>" (re-titled "So Much Pain"). The rappers felt Ja Rule could not compare to Tupac, and so they made the track, mocking him for trying to "imitate" the deceased rap icon.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> Eminem prevented Ja Rule from appearing on any of the "new" Tupac songs he produced, including those on <i><a href="/wiki/Loyal_to_the_Game" title="Loyal to the Game">Loyal to the Game</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-eminem.net_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-eminem.net-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="DMX">DMX</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ja_Rule&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: DMX">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After <a href="/wiki/Murder_Inc._(rap_group)" title="Murder Inc. (rap group)">Murder Inc.</a> broke up in 1999 due to animosity between <a href="/wiki/DMX_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="DMX (rapper)">DMX</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a>, DMX accused Ja Rule of copying his signature "gruff style", and the two subsequently fell out. On the single "<a href="/wiki/Where_the_Hood_At%3F" title="Where the Hood At?">Where the Hood At?</a>", DMX disses Ja Rule by replicating lyrics from other Ja Rule songs, referring to Ja Rule's controversy of being labeled as <a href="/wiki/Homophobia" title="Homophobia">homophobic</a> in the lyrics such as "I show no love to <a href="/wiki/Homosexuality" title="Homosexuality">homo</a> thugs" or "Last time I checked, you <a href="/wiki/Nigga" title="Nigga">niggas</a> <a href="/wiki/Gay_sexual_practices" title="Gay sexual practices">having sex with the same sex</a>".<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Ja Rule responded with several disses on his album, <i>Blood in My Eye</i>, including "Clap Back".<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> DMX said that he wanted the dispute to end when he was released from jail in 2005: "<a href="/wiki/Irv_Gotti" title="Irv Gotti">[Irv] Gotti</a> came to me in jail and said I want to make peace with you and him. I was like, 'All right, Gotti, let's do it man."<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> DMX and Ja Rule finally ended their feud at VH1's 2009 Hip Hop Honors.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Kurupt">Kurupt</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ja_Rule&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Kurupt">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>By his association with <a href="/wiki/DMX_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="DMX (rapper)">DMX</a>, Ja Rule was brought into the beef between DMX and <a href="/wiki/Kurupt" title="Kurupt">Kurupt</a>, being dissed on Kurupt's 1999 song "Callin' Out Names". Ja Rule responded with "Still INC" featuring <a href="/wiki/Black_Child_(rapper)" class="mw-redirect" title="Black Child (rapper)">Black Child</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cadillac_Tah" class="mw-redirect" title="Cadillac Tah">Cadillac Tah</a>, a freestyle over <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Still_D.R.E." title="Still D.R.E.">Still D.R.E.</a>" beat. The two eventually squashed their beef on the set of the movie <i><a href="/wiki/Half_Past_Dead" title="Half Past Dead">Half Past Dead</a></i> in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foxy_Brown">Foxy Brown</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ja_Rule&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Foxy Brown">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In October 2002, rapper <a href="/wiki/Foxy_Brown_(rapper)" title="Foxy Brown (rapper)">Foxy Brown</a> dismissed reports of recording a track with rivals <a href="/wiki/Nas" title="Nas">Nas</a> and Ja Rule that was "potentially" deprecatory of Jay-Z.<sup id="cite_ref-feds_123-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-feds-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> During a Thanksgiving week interview in 2002, while on <i>Doug Banks In the Morning</i>, Ja Rule stated that he "[couldn't] stand Foxy Brown."<sup id="cite_ref-MTV4_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV4-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-yt4_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yt4-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> Brown reportedly heard Ja Rule's comments via a radio while she was helping her mother clean her house.<sup id="cite_ref-yt4_125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yt4-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> Going against her manager's wishes, during her own interview with <a href="/wiki/Doug_Banks" title="Doug Banks">Doug Banks</a>, Brown informed Banks that she was "flabbergasted" by Rule's comments.<sup id="cite_ref-yt4_125-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yt4-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> Brown explained she was particularly angry at Rule's response, having never met him.<sup id="cite_ref-yt4_125-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yt4-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The incident provoked Brown to record the unreleased, "Get Off Me".<sup id="cite_ref-MTV4_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV4-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sohh2_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sohh2-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> In the record, Brown targeted Ja Rule and <a href="/wiki/Eve_(entertainer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Eve (entertainer)">Eve</a> with homophobic remarks.<sup id="cite_ref-MTV4_124-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV4-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sohh2_126-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sohh2-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> In 2005, Ja Rule and his two bodyguards were initial suspects in the killing of Willie "Willie Bang Bang" Clark, whom authorities linked as a "revenge" that stemmed back to a robbery case involving Foxy Brown's brother.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2009, Ja Rule and Foxy Brown ended their beef at the <a href="/wiki/VH1" title="VH1">VH1</a> <a href="/wiki/Hip_Hop_Honors" title="Hip Hop Honors">Hip Hop Honors</a>, where they celebrated the twenty-fifth anniversary of their former label, Def Jam Recordings.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> The feud was squashed after both rappers shared a photo with ex-labelmates DMX and <a href="/wiki/Ludacris" title="Ludacris">Ludacris</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Lil.27_Mo"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Lil'_Mo">Lil' Mo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ja_Rule&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Lil&#039; Mo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In January 2003, while co-hosting <i><a href="/wiki/106_%26_Park" title="106 &amp; Park">106 &amp; Park: Prime</a></i>, singer <a href="/wiki/Lil%27_Mo" title="Lil&#39; Mo">Lil' Mo</a> sent a shout-out to <a href="/wiki/50_Cent" title="50 Cent">50 Cent</a>, just seconds after she premiered a Ja Rule video.<sup id="cite_ref-vibe_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vibe-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> Ja Rule and the Murda, Inc., clique were outraged.<sup id="cite_ref-vibe_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vibe-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> In response, Ja Rule released "Loose Change", a track deprecatory of <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a>, 50 Cent, <a href="/wiki/Dr._Dre" title="Dr. Dre">Dr. Dre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Lighty" title="Chris Lighty">Chris Lighty</a> and Lil' Mo.<sup id="cite_ref-MTV4_124-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV4-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-vibe_131-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vibe-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> Rule rechristened Mo a "bitch", and credited himself with causing her popularity.<sup id="cite_ref-MTV6_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV6-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> In May 2003, Mo released a freestyle track attacking Ja Rule, where she interpolated the "Used to be my homie, used to be my ace, now I can't stand you, yeah I wanna slap the taste out your mouth." lyrics Dr. Dre used in his 1993 <a href="/wiki/Eazy-E" title="Eazy-E">Eazy-E</a> <a href="/wiki/Diss_(music)" title="Diss (music)">diss track</a> "<a href="/wiki/Fuck_wit_Dre_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="Fuck wit Dre Day">Fuck wit Dre Day</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2003, Lil' Mo sparked additional controversy, complaining of receiving neither recognition nor payment for her contributions to Rule's records "<a href="/wiki/I_Cry_(Ja_Rule_song)" title="I Cry (Ja Rule song)">I Cry</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Put_It_on_Me_(Ja_Rule_song)" title="Put It on Me (Ja Rule song)">Put It on Me</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-MTV2_134-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV2-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> Mo told <i><a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV News</a></i>, "Those two records ["I Cry", "Put It on Me"] ruled 2001. The whole world knows that ... If I speak the truth, I can't apologize. I helped that brother sell 3 million records, and I don't have a plaque [for <i><a href="/wiki/Rule_3:36" title="Rule 3:36">Rule 3:36</a></i>]."<sup id="cite_ref-MTV2_134-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV2-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> By way of contrast, she highlighted <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a>'s having given her recognition, a plaque, a thank you card and a bottle of <a href="/wiki/Cristal_(wine)" title="Cristal (wine)">Cristal</a> for her work on his "Parking Lot Pimpin'".<sup id="cite_ref-MTV2_134-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MTV2-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> In 2005, Lil' Mo filed a lawsuit against Ja Rule, Murda Inc. and <a href="/wiki/Def_Jam_Records" class="mw-redirect" title="Def Jam Records">Def Jam Records</a> for over $15 million.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> In 2010, the two reconciled.<sup id="cite_ref-yt2_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yt2-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> Lil' Mo stated that she ended the dispute as Ja Rule's career was in decline and noted that "life is too short ... You just never know what people are going through."<sup id="cite_ref-yt2_136-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-yt2-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, the two reunited and recorded a track together titled, "U &amp; Me".<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_nominations">Awards and nominations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ja_Rule&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Awards and nominations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<dl><dt><a href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards" title="American Music Awards">American Music Awards</a></dt></dl>
